## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is the acceleration of a particle/degree-of-freedom governed by an oscillator equation, with state variables x (position) and v (velocity) evolving in time t. Common models express dv_dt as restoring forces in x plus damping/forcing terms in v and t, often including nonlinear stiffness or nonlinear damping.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = -c0 * x (linear restoring acceleration)
- Linear damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Phase-shifted harmonic forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (general sinusoidal drive)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x^3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x^3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear stiffness + drive)
- Pendulum (nonlinear restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v (large-angle oscillator approximation)
- Pendulum with periodic torque: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator (nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x^2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited limit cycle dynamics)
- Rayleigh oscillator (nonlinear damping in v): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * v - c2 * v^3 (velocity-dependent pumping and saturation)
- Liénard-type polynomial model: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x^3 - (c2 + c3 * x^2) * v (combined nonlinear stiffness and x-dependent damping)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness / parametric resonance)
- Nonlinear stiffness with higher-order terms: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x^3 - c2 * x^5 - c3 * v (strongly nonlinear springs)
- State-dependent frequency (amplitude-dependent restoring): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * x^2) * x - c2 * v (effective stiffness increases with amplitude)
- Nonlinear friction (Coulomb-like smooth approximation): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * tanh(c2 * v) (dry-friction-like damping without discontinuity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring forces → dv_dt primarily a function of x (e.g., odd stiffness terms like -c*x, -c*x^3, or -c*sin(x)); minimal direct dependence on t and v.
- Viscous damping → additive term proportional to velocity, typically -c*v, producing amplitude decay and a spiral toward equilibrium in phase space.
- Self-excited oscillations / limit cycles → negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, often captured by (1 - c*x^2)*v or v - c*v^3 terms.
- Hardening/softening spring behavior → inclusion of x^3 (and higher odd powers) shifts frequency with amplitude; sign of the cubic term distinguishes hardening vs softening.
- Geometric nonlinearity (pendulum-like) → sin(x) restoring term; for small x it linearizes to -c*x, while for larger x it yields amplitude-dependent period.
- External periodic drive → explicit t-dependence via sin(c*t) or cos(c*t), producing resonance peaks and possibly chaotic responses when combined with nonlinearity.
- Parametric resonance → stiffness modulated by time, appearing as cos(c*t)*x (multiplicative coupling of t and x), leading to instability tongues in parameter space.
- Nonlinear friction / saturation of damping → tanh(c*v), v*Abs(v), or polynomial v - c*v^3 shapes limit high-speed damping and can mimic dry friction or aerodynamic drag.
- Equilibrium shifts / bias forces → constant or slowly varying additive terms in dv_dt (e.g., +c or +c*cos(c*t)) change the center of oscillation or create asymmetric motion.

Variables participate as: v enters via |v| and v^3; t enters linearly, inside log(1+c5 t), and inside exp(c7 t); x enters as (c8+1)*x plus c9*x/(|x|+1)^3. With fitted values, the x-part is approximately -(1.0172)x since c8≈-2.017 and the rational correction is tiny (c9≈0.017); the time terms are modest (c1≈-0.033, log coefficient c4≈-0.070 small, and c6 exp(c7 t) is a decaying negative transient because c6<0 and c7≈-1.04). But GT needs \(\sin(t)\) (not present), needs \(\log(|v|+1)\) (candidate log depends on \(t\), not \(v\)), and needs the \(v(1-x^2)\) polynomial coupling (absent). Cannot.

No candidate contains simultaneously:
- \(\sin(t)\) as an additive term independent of \(x\),
- \(\log(|v|+1)\) (log in \(v\) with Abs),
- and the coupled \( -a v + a v x^2\) structure.

Therefore none can be parameter-tuned to equal the GT globally.

GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - beta*sin(v) - c1*beta*v - mu*(c2 - x**c3)*v
Candidates evaluated: 50

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.118064*v*(1 - x²) - 1.00534*v - 0.502671*log(|v| + 1) + 0.342319*sin(t) - 0.502671*sin(v)`

Expanding: `-0.118064*v + 0.118064*v*x² - 1.00534*v - 0.502671*log(|v| + 1) + 0.342319*sin(t) - 0.502671*sin(v)`

Simplifying: `0.118064*v*x² - 1.12340*v - 0.502671*log(|v| + 1) + 0.342319*sin(t) - 0.502671*sin(v)`

The GT contains these basis functions:
1. `v*x²` - product of v and x²
2. `v` - linear in v
3. `log(|v| + 1)` - logarithm involving v
4. `sin(t)` - sine of t
5. `sin(v)` - sine of v

Key observations:
- The GT has `sin(t)` and `sin(v)` terms - these are transcendental functions that cannot be replicated by polynomials, exponentials, or logarithms.
- Most candidates use `log(c*t + 1)` and `exp(c*t)` for the t-dependence, which cannot exactly equal `sin(t)`.
- Most candidates lack `sin(v)` entirely.
- The `log(|v| + 1)` term is specific and most candidates use `|v|` instead.

Let me check if any candidate has both `sin(t)` and `sin(v)`:

**Candidate 50:** `c0*x + c1*Abs(v) + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5 + c6*log(c7*t + 1) + c8*exp(c9*t)`

This has `sin(c3*v + c4)` which could give `sin(v)` terms, but it uses `log(c7*t+1)` and `exp(c9*t)` for t-dependence instead of `sin(t)`. These cannot equal `sin(t)`. **NO MATCH.**

No candidate has `sin(t)` as a basis function. The candidates use combinations of `t`, `log(c*t+1)`, and `exp(c*t)` for t-dependence. None of these can exactly reproduce `sin(t)` - a periodic function cannot be expressed as a combination of monotonic functions (linear, log, exponential).

Similarly, `sin(v)` appears in the GT but almost no candidate has it (except Candidate 50 which has `sin(v)` but lacks `sin(t)`).

Since `sin(t)` is an essential, non-zero term (coefficient ≈ 0.342) and cannot be replicated by any combination of `t`, `log(t+c)`, `exp(ct)`, polynomials, etc., **no candidate can match the GT**.

Let me verify Candidate 50 more carefully: it has `sin(c3*v+c4)` but needs `sin(t)` which it replaces with `log` and `exp` of t. Still no match.

Going through all 50 candidates systematically - none contain `sin(t)` as a basis function, and the coefficient 0.342319 is non-zero, so this term cannot be eliminated. Therefore, no candidate matches.
